</div><div class="mw-content-ltr mw-parser-output" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Multilingual lexical-semantic knowledge graph and encyclopedic dictionary</div>

<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Machine-readable_dictionary" title="Machine-readable dictionary">Multilingual encyclopedic dictionary</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Linked_data" title="Linked data">Linked data</a></li></ul>
</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space: nowrap;"><a href="/wiki/Software_license" title="Software license">License</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Attribution-NonCommercial-ShareAlike_3.0_Unported" class="mw-redirect" title="Attribution-NonCommercial-ShareAlike 3.0 Unported">Attribution-NonCommercial-ShareAlike 3.0 Unported</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space: nowrap;">Website</th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://babelnet.org/">babelnet<wbr>.org</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>BabelNet</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Multilinguality" class="mw-redirect" title="Multilinguality">multilingual</a> lexical-semantic <a href="/wiki/Knowledge_graph" title="Knowledge graph">knowledge graph</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ontology_(information_science)" title="Ontology (information science)">ontology</a> and encyclopedic <a href="/wiki/Dictionary" title="Dictionary">dictionary</a> developed at the <a href="/wiki/Natural_Language_Processing" class="mw-redirect" title="Natural Language Processing">NLP</a> group of the <a href="/wiki/Sapienza_University_of_Rome" title="Sapienza University of Rome">Sapienza University of Rome</a> under the supervision of <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Navigli" title="Roberto Navigli">Roberto Navigli</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NavigliPonzetto12_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NavigliPonzetto12-1"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> BabelNet was automatically created by linking <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia" title="Wikipedia">Wikipedia</a> to the most popular computational <a href="/wiki/Dictionary" title="Dictionary">lexicon</a> of the <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English language</a>, <a href="/wiki/WordNet" title="WordNet">WordNet</a>. The integration is done using an automatic mapping and by filling in lexical gaps in resource-poor <a href="/wiki/Language" title="Language">languages</a> by using <a href="/wiki/Statistical_machine_translation" title="Statistical machine translation">statistical machine translation</a>. The result is an <a href="/wiki/Encyclopedic_dictionary" title="Encyclopedic dictionary">encyclopedic dictionary</a> that provides <a href="/wiki/Concept" title="Concept">concepts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Named_entity" title="Named entity">named entities</a> <a href="/wiki/Lexicalization" title="Lexicalization">lexicalized</a> in many languages and connected with large amounts of <a href="/wiki/Semantic_relation#Relationships" class="mw-redirect" title="Semantic relation">semantic relations</a>. Additional lexicalizations and definitions are added by linking to free-license wordnets, OmegaWiki, the English <a href="/wiki/Wiktionary" title="Wiktionary">Wiktionary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wikidata" title="Wikidata">Wikidata</a>, <a href="/wiki/FrameNet" title="FrameNet">FrameNet</a>, <a href="/wiki/VerbNet" title="VerbNet">VerbNet</a> and others. Similarly to WordNet, BabelNet groups <a href="/wiki/Word" title="Word">words</a> in different languages into sets of <a href="/wiki/Synonyms" class="mw-redirect" title="Synonyms">synonyms</a>, called <i>Babel <a href="/wiki/Synsets" class="mw-redirect" title="Synsets">synsets</a></i>. For each Babel synset, BabelNet provides short definitions (called <a href="/wiki/Definition" title="Definition">glosses</a>) in many languages harvested from both WordNet and Wikipedia.
</p>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:The_BabelNet_structure.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/The_BabelNet_structure.png/960px-The_BabelNet_structure.png" decoding="async" width="600" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/The_BabelNet_structure.png/1280px-The_BabelNet_structure.png 2x" data-file-width="1313" data-file-height="362"></a><figcaption>BabelNet is a multilingual semantic network obtained as an integration of WordNet and Wikipedia.</figcaption></figure>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc">
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Statistics_of_BabelNet">Statistics of BabelNet</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BabelNet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Statistics of BabelNet"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>As of December&nbsp;2023<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=BabelNet&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, BabelNet (version 5.3) covers 600 <a href="/wiki/Language" title="Language">languages</a>. It contains almost 23 million synsets and around 1.7 billion <a href="/wiki/Word_sense" title="Word sense">word senses</a> (regardless of their language). Each Babel synset contains 2 synonyms per language, i.e., word senses, on average. The semantic network includes all the lexico-semantic relations from WordNet (<a href="/wiki/Hyponymy" class="mw-redirect" title="Hyponymy">hypernymy and hyponymy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meronymy" class="mw-redirect" title="Meronymy">meronymy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Holonymy" class="mw-redirect" title="Holonymy">holonymy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antonymy" class="mw-redirect" title="Antonymy">antonymy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Synonymy" class="mw-redirect" title="Synonymy">synonymy</a>, etc., totaling around 364,000 relation edges) as well as an underspecified relatedness relation from Wikipedia (totaling around 1.9 billion edges).<sup id="cite_ref-NavigliPonzetto12_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NavigliPonzetto12-1"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Version 5.3 also associates around 61 million images with Babel synsets and provides a Lemon <a href="/wiki/Resource_Description_Framework" title="Resource Description Framework">RDF</a> encoding of the resource,<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> available via a <a href="/wiki/SPARQL_endpoint" class="mw-redirect" title="SPARQL endpoint">SPARQL endpoint</a>. 2.67 million synsets are assigned domain labels.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Applications">Applications</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BabelNet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Applications"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>BabelNet has been shown to enable multilingual <a href="/wiki/Natural_language_processing" title="Natural language processing">natural language processing</a> applications. The lexicalized <a href="/wiki/Knowledge" title="Knowledge">knowledge</a> available in BabelNet has been shown to obtain state-of-the-art results in:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Semantic_relatedness" class="mw-redirect" title="Semantic relatedness">Semantic relatedness</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Multilingual <a href="/wiki/Word-sense_disambiguation" title="Word-sense disambiguation">word-sense disambiguation</a><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Entity_linking" title="Entity linking">entity linking</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/Babelfy" title="Babelfy">Babelfy</a> system,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Game_with_a_purpose" class="mw-redirect" title="Game with a purpose">Video games with a purpose</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Prizes_and_acknowledgments">Prizes and acknowledgments</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=BabelNet&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Prizes and acknowledgments"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>BabelNet received the META prize 2015 for "groundbreaking work in overcoming language barriers through a multilingual lexicalised semantic network and ontology making use of heterogeneous data sources".
</p><p>The Artificial Intelligence Journal paper that describes BabelNet<sup id="cite_ref-NavigliPonzetto12_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NavigliPonzetto12-1"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> won the Prominent Paper Award in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-aij_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aij-9"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>BabelNet featured prominently in a <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> magazine article<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> about the new age of innovative and up-to-date lexical knowledge resources available on the Web.
</p>

<div class="rt-overlay"></div><div id="mw-teleport-target" class="vector-body"></div><a accesskey="v" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BabelNet?action=edit" class="oo-ui-element-hidden"></a><div style="all: initial; position: fixed !important; display: block !important; z-index: 2147483647 !important"></div></body></html>
GOLD:
BabelNet is a multilingual lexical-semantic knowledge graph, ontology and encyclopedic dictionary developed at the NLP group of the Sapienza University of Rome under the supervision of Roberto Navigli. BabelNet was automatically created by linking Wikipedia to the most popular computational lexicon of the English language, WordNet. The integration is done using an automatic mapping and by filling in lexical gaps in resource-poor languages by using statistical machine translation. The result is an encyclopedic dictionary that provides concepts and named entities lexicalized in many languages and connected with large amounts of semantic relations. Additional lexicalizations and definitions are added by linking to free-license wordnets, OmegaWiki, the English Wiktionary, Wikidata, FrameNet, VerbNet and others. Similarly to WordNet, BabelNet groups words in different languages into sets of synonyms, called Babelsynsets. For each Babel synset, BabelNet provides short definitions (called glosses) in many languages harvested from both WordNet and Wikipedia.

Statistics of BabelNet
As of December 2023, BabelNet (version 5.3) covers 600 languages. It contains almost 23 million synsets and around 1.7 billion word senses (regardless of their language). Each Babel synset contains 2 synonyms per language, i.e., word senses, on average. The semantic network includes all the lexico-semantic relations from WordNet (hypernymy and hyponymy, meronymy and holonymy, antonymy and synonymy, etc., totaling around 364,000 relation edges) as well as an underspecified relatedness relation from Wikipedia (totaling around 1.9 billion edges). Version 5.3 also associates around 61 million images with Babel synsets and provides a Lemon RDF encoding of the resource, available via a SPARQL endpoint. 2.67 million synsets are assigned domain labels.

Applications
BabelNet has been shown to enable multilingual natural language processing applications. The lexicalized knowledge available in BabelNet has been shown to obtain state-of-the-art results in:

Semantic relatedness,
Multilingual word-sense disambiguation and entity linking, with the Babelfy system,
Video games with a purpose.

Prizes and acknowledgments
BabelNet received the META prize 2015 for "groundbreaking work in overcoming language barriers through a multilingual lexicalised semantic network and ontology making use of heterogeneous data sources".
The Artificial Intelligence Journal paper that describes BabelNet won the Prominent Paper Award in 2017.
BabelNet featured prominently in a Time magazine article about the new age of innovative and up-to-date lexical knowledge resources available on the Web.
